## da7332ec -- Actually handling nested interrupts and introducing kernel
   threads (#26)

Commit: da7332ec38...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Apr 17 19:01:51 2017 +0300

Message:

  This huge change actually makes nested interrupts to be handled
  correctly (hopefully!) and introduces kernel threads, with all the
  special code for handling them. Along with that, tons of small bugs
  have been fixed and many improvements have been added as well as a
  side-effect of the whole work, like the panic handling and dump of
  backtraces that now cannot cause page faults since checks with
  is_mapped() each pointer before de-referencing it.

  Kernel tasklets have been just introduced as well, along with unit
  tests which, as a side-effect, improved the whole testing
  infrastructure as well.

  Final note: this change fixes also a nasty bug preventing the
  bootloader to actually load stage2+kernel on real hardware due to
  a wrong number of cylinders in the fatpart. See the change in its
  script.

AI notes:

What changed:

  Huge PR (41 files, +1359 / -491). The three load-bearing pieces:

  - Nested-interrupt handling: kernel/arch/i386/idt.c (+67 / -33)
    and kernel/arch/i386/irq.c (+79 / -49) track an interrupt-depth
    counter; re-entering the handler via a nested IRQ behaves
    correctly. kernel/arch/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+83 / -72) reworks
    the stub so the regs struct on the stack is correct even under
    nesting.

  - Kernel threads: kernel/process.c (+119 / -39), kernel/
    arch/i386/process32.c (+56 / -10), kernel/include/process.h
    (+14 / -7) -- the task-info machinery generalizes: processes
    and kernel threads share the struct; a "kthread_create" path
    sets up the process_info + pdir (shared kernel pdir) and
    inserts it in the scheduler ring.

  - Tasklets: new kernel/tasklet.c (82 l.) + kernel/include/tasklet.h
    (33 l.). Ring-buffer of MAX_TASKLETS=1024 deferred-work items;
    add_tasklet3(f, a1, a2, a3) enqueues, run_one_tasklet() dequeues
    one and runs it in process context. Interrupt handlers can defer
    heavy work to a kernel thread this way. Arg-count variants
    add_tasklet0..3 are macros on a common add_tasklet_int.

  - New unittests/tasklet_test.cpp (190 l.) -- gtest coverage for
    the tasklet primitives.

  - kernel/debug_utils.c (+52 / -35) -- dump_stacktrace() now
    bounds-checks every frame pointer with is_mapped() before
    dereferencing, so a corrupted frame doesn't cause a secondary
    page fault during a panic.

  - Rename: kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/utils.h ->
    x86_utils.h. Rename: kernel/include/arch_utils.h -> hal.h
    (first appearance of the "HAL" name -- Hardware Abstraction
    Layer).

  - New kernel/misc.c (5 l.) -- placeholder for miscellaneous
    helpers.

  - build_scripts/build_fatpart.sh (+4 / -4) -- corrects the FAT
    geometry (-T value) so real-hardware BIOSes can CHS-load the
    full image. Previously some machines would read only the
    first few tracks.

  - New qemu_img_create_vmdk.sh (3 l.) -- dev helper script.

  - Many other files: kernel/main.c (+38 / -34), kernel/timer.c
    (+30 / -20), kernel/syscalls.c (+4 / -3), kernel/kmalloc.c
    (+8 / -6), unittests/CMakeLists.txt (+2), etc.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Transitions the kernel from "cooperative scheduler with implicit
  trust in interrupt paths" to something that starts to resemble a
  real preemptive kernel. Kernel threads + tasklets are the
  foundations for scheduled background work (block-io callbacks,
  deferred page-fault resolution, etc.).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d6ac2e2d -- Introducing kernel preemption for user processes (#27)

Commit: d6ac2e2d16...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Apr 30 15:17:54 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change makes each user thread to have its own kernel stack,
  that will be used by the kernel when an interrupt (or syscall)
  occurs. That code runs by default with preemption disabled but it
  can be enabled as well, as happens in the DEMO implementation of
  sys_waitpid(). Therefore, the kernel can actually preempt itself
  and correctly account the ticks that it spent working on a job
  for a user process. In addition to that, a kernel_yield()
  function has been added. That function allows kernel code to save
  its current state and call the scheduler. Overall, all that
  brings exOS much closer to modern operating systems like Linux.

  [plus a 15-bullet commit-by-commit log ending in: implementing
  kernel_yield and making printk disable preemption.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/process.c (+205 / -47), kernel/arch/i386/process32.c
    (+50 / -35) -- each task gets its own kernel stack allocated at
    task-create; the TSS is updated before context-switching into a
    task so any ring transition (int, syscall) lands on that task's
    kernel stack instead of a shared one.

  - kernel_yield() -- kernel-side cooperative yield: saves the
    caller's state into the task struct and calls schedule(). Unlike
    a regular schedule after interrupt, this works from arbitrary
    kernel code. Enables code like sys_waitpid() to block without
    holding the CPU.

  - kernel/arch/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+70 / -18) -- asm support for the
    new kernel-stack-per-task model and for kernel_yield.

  - running_in_kernel flag + preemption-enabled / disabled nesting
    counter, maintained across nested interrupts so accounting
    stays correct.

  - Tick accounting: timer_ticks splits into "kernel" vs "user"
    ticks per task, so top-like tools can eventually report CPU
    usage. process.c's counters are reset on task destroy.

  - kernel/main.c (+27 / -26), kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+3 / -3),
    kernel/include/arch/i386/arch_utils.h (+31 / -17),
    kernel/include/arch/i386/process_int.h (+6 / -3),
    kernel/include/process.h (+15 / -8), kernel/timer.c (+11 / -9),
    usermode_init/init.c (+5) -- matching plumbing. printk() now
    disables preemption around VGA writes to avoid tearing.

Context (PR body):

  Foundation for true preemptive multitasking: a user task can now
  be preempted even while the CPU is running kernel code on its
  behalf. Previously kernel code was effectively non-preemptible,
  making long syscalls (like waitpid) a CPU hog.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## f2495348 -- Sync primitives (#29)

Commit: f249534899...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat May 6 12:56:51 2017 +0300

Message:

  Adding the first kernel synchronization primitive, kmutex, and a
  ton of other minor fixes, especially related with tests.

  [plus a 19-bullet single-commit log.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/kmutex.c (96 l.) + kernel/include/sync.h (43 l.) --
    first kernel synchronization primitive: a non-recursive mutex
    backed by the scheduler's wait-on-object mechanism.

      * wait_obj { type, ptr } lets a task sleep on a kmutex without
        the kmutex code knowing about scheduler internals.
      * kmutex_init / lock / trylock / unlock / kmutex_destroy.
      * Asserts against re-entrant lock by the same task (so the
        author can find accidental recursion bugs early).

  - New kernel/interrupts.c (98 l.) -- consolidates the
    interrupt-depth tracking extracted from arch/i386/idt.c (-98).

  - New kernel/sched.c (304 l.) -- pulls the scheduler out of
    process.c (-282). kernel/process.c (+20 / -282) now holds just
    the task-struct management; sched.c has the run-queue and
    schedule() logic.

  - New kernel/mm.c (10 l.) -- placeholder for arch-independent
    memory-management helpers.

  - Files moved: kernel/perftests.c -> kernel/test_stuff/perftests.c
    (same for perftests_data.c).

  - New kernel/test_stuff/testrunners.c (103 l.) -- in-kernel test
    harness entry points, plus dummy tasklet handlers that fire
    when special keypresses arrive.

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+20 / -14) -- initialize_kmalloc() now
    bzero()s allocation_for_metadata_nodes, fixing an intermittent
    test-side bug caused by garbage in the bitmap.

  - unittests/ -- kmalloc / asm_mocks / kernel_init_funcs updates
    (+21 / -11 and similar) to get the tests building and passing
    again after the sched split.

  - Plus various small fixes: kernel pages globally mapped (paging.c
    +5 / -18), schedule_outside_interrupt_context(), bzero() helper
    in string_util.c, and misc tasklet test triggers.

Context (PR body = 19-commit log):

  This is the PR that takes process.c from "everything lives here"
  to sched.c + process.c + sync.h + kmutex.c + interrupts.c + mm.c
  + test_stuff/. The logical split maps to the file split; each
  piece becomes independently reviewable for the first time.

## 04e1776d -- Adding condition variables and improving the scheduler (#32)

Commit: 04e1776d8f...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon May 8 11:47:48 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change adds condition variables to the kernel and use them
  for the tasklet runner kthread. In addition to that, it
  introduces:
    - the idle_task_kthread which is definitive solution for what
      the scheduler should do when there's just nothing to do (no
      runnable tasks).
    - the "state lists" and the function task_change_state() and
      making the all the code iterating tasks to use them, when
      possible. This means cycling only through runnable tasks for
      the scheduler and cycling only through sleeping tasks for
      kmutex and kcond.

  [plus 8-bullet single-commit log.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/kcond.c (70 l.) + include changes to kernel/include/
    sync.h (+51 / -8): kcond_init / kcond_wait(c, m) / kcond_signal
    / kcond_broadcast (the full pthread_cond-style API). Tasks
    waiting on a kcond sleep on a wait_obj of type WOBJ_KCOND.

  - kernel/tasklet.c (+34 / -18) -- the tasklet-runner kthread now
    sleeps on a kcond; add_tasklet_int() signals it. Replaces the
    busy-wait / sleep(1) pattern.

  - kernel/sched.c (+80 / -31) -- introduces **state lists**: a
    separate linked list per task state (RUNNABLE, SLEEPING,
    ZOMBIE). task_change_state(t, new_state) moves a task between
    lists. schedule() iterates only the runnable list; kmutex and
    kcond iterate only the sleeping list looking for tasks waiting
    on them.

  - idle_task_kthread: runs HLT in a loop; schedule() picks it when
    no other runnable task exists. Replaces the earlier "loop with
    interrupts on" idle approach.

  - kernel/kmutex.c (+26 / -26) -- owner / wait-list updated to
    use state lists; owner handling is cleaner.

  - kernel/main.c (-22), kernel/process.c (+8 / -3), kernel/
    arch/i386/process32.c (1 l.),
    kernel/include/arch/i386/arch_utils.h (+6 / -2),
    kernel/include/arch/i386/process_int.h (+4 / -1),
    kernel/include/process.h (+10 / -1),
    kernel/include/tasklet.h (+2 / -1) -- matching plumbing.

  - kernel/test_stuff/testrunners.c (+76 / -11) -- kcond smoke
    tests.

  - unittests/generic_mocks.c (+10), asm_mocks.c (+5 / -5) --
    mocks for the new kthread_create path.

  - Child of fork() changed to start in RUNNABLE rather than
    RUNNING state, matching how schedule() picks it up.

Context (PR body is the commit log):

  Scheduler now has proper O(runnable) scan, real condition
  variables, and a dedicated idle task. Closer to Linux in both API
  surface and internal structure.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 2019c26c -- Adding (incomplete) kernel timers and improving the handling of
   the idle task (#33)

Commit: 2019c26cd3...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue May 16 20:07:59 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change adds a basic (incomplete) implementation of kernel
  timers [allowing kernel_sleep()] and improves a lot of the way
  the idle task works. Now, in no case the idle task will be
  scheduled if there is anything runnable.

  In addition, the "current_task" variable has been renamed to
  "current", following the convention of the Linux kernel.

  Other: this change contains several bug fixes, like the one not
  allowing the init process to exit gracefully due to an attempt
  by the kernel to kfree() a page table not allocated with
  kmalloc().

  [plus 16-bullet single-commit log.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/timer.c (+69) -- kthread_timer_sleep_obj slots
    (timers_array[64]) pairing a ticks-to-sleep counter with a
    task_info*. register_curr_task_for_timer_sleep(ticks) grabs a
    slot, marks the current task TASK_STATE_SLEEPING.
    tick_all_timers() (called from timer_handler context) decrements
    each slot's counter; slots that hit 0 transition their task back
    to RUNNABLE and force a context switch. New kernel_sleep(ticks)
    entry point wraps register + yield.

  - kernel/sched.c (+115 / -59) -- runnable_tasks_count added; the
    idle task yields as soon as runnable_tasks_count > 0. schedule()
    no longer has the "if selected == current, skip" branch (the
    root cause of a subtle bug where schedule was stomping its own
    stack; switch is always done via explicit switch_to_task()).

  - current_task global renamed to current throughout (matching
    Linux's convention -- `current` is the canonical macro for
    "current task").

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+22 / -12) -- bug fix: page tables
    for the init pdir are allocated via paging_alloc_pageframe(),
    not kmalloc(); pdir_destroy() now frees them through the right
    path. Previously init's exit triggered a kfree() on a
    pageframe-allocator page, corrupting the heap.

  - kernel/test_stuff/testrunners.c (+25 / -2) -- smoke test for
    kernel_sleep.

  - kernel/kcond.c (+3 / -1), kernel/kmutex.c (+3 / -1),
    kernel/process.c (+10 / -17), kernel/main.c (+4 / -15),
    kernel/debug_utils.c (+5 / -5), kernel/interrupts.c (1 l.),
    kernel/include/common_defs.h (+12 / -4),
    kernel/include/process.h (+10 / -4), kernel/include/hal.h
    (+1), kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/x86_utils.h (+28 / -17),
    usermode_init/init.c (+5 / -5) -- plumbing.

Context (PR body + log):

  Lands three major fixes simultaneously: working kernel_sleep for
  time-based task wakeups, a proper idle-task policy (never runs
  while something else can), and the init-exit corruption fix. The
  "current" rename is the first of several conventions pulled in
  from the Linux kernel's style.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 8ec2e77d -- Introducing system testing (#34)

Commit: 8ec2e77da6...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed May 17 19:56:01 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change makes exOS to write on the serial port COM1 everything
  that it shown on the screen and introduces an actual basic system
  test written in python that checks (for now) that no kernel panic
  or reboot occurred. In addition, the new system test has been
  integrated to run in Travis as well.

  [plus 7-bullet single-commit log: serial output, qemu-exit for
  testing, renaming tests target to gtests, native python system
  test, timeout, runner improvements, wiring in Travis.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  First system test infrastructure.

  - kernel/term.c (+52 / -14) -- adds init_serial_port() that
    programs COM1 (divisor 3, 38400 baud, 8N1, FIFO, IRQs enabled).
    term_write_char() now mirrors every byte to the serial port via
    write_serial(). Gives Travis a way to capture kernel output
    without a VGA framebuffer.

  - New kernel/include/config.h (12 l.) -- first config.h file with
    two DEBUG_QEMU_EXIT_ON_* macros. When defined, init's exit() and
    panic() trigger outw(0xf4, 0) which, combined with qemu's
    -device isa-debug-exit,iobase=0xf4, exits the VM with a
    well-defined status code.

  - kernel/process.c (+11), kernel/main.c (+5 / -3) -- hook the
    qemu-exit into the init-exit path.

  - New system_tests/run_system_test (89 l.) -- python script that
    boots the kernel under qemu with serial redirected to stdout,
    captures the output, checks for absence of "KERNEL_PANIC" and
    absence of machine resets within a configurable timeout,
    propagates qemu's exit code.

  - .travis.yml (+10 / -6) -- adds qemu-system-i386 to apt packages;
    runs run_system_test in the script: phase.

  - build_toolchain (+5 / -2), unittests/CMakeLists.txt (+6 / -6),
    kernel/debug_utils.c (+8 / -1), kernel/include/common_defs.h
    (+1), kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/x86_utils.h (+4) --
    plumbing.

Context (PR body + commit log):

  Unit tests covered kernel-subsystem logic; system tests now cover
  kernel-as-a-VM behavior. Boot-to-panic in CI goes from "maybe it
  works on someone's laptop" to a machine-verifiable pass/fail.

## 83f95ad5 -- Bug fixing (#36)

Commit: 83f95ad52a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue May 23 21:28:40 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change fixes a ton of nasty bugs, in particular one bug in
  kernel_yield: see the comments in its body for details. In
  addition, several constraints have been added, allowing more
  robust code to be written in the future.

  [plus 15-bullet single-commit log.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  Big bug-fix PR (29 files, +362 / -164). Notable pieces:

  - kernel/sched.c (+51 / -29) -- kernel_yield bug: the idle task's
    halt() was running BEFORE the idle_ticks++ inside the loop, so
    after wake-up from HLT the counter update could race with timer
    tick code running on the same task. Reordered to increment
    first, then halt. Also: kernel_yield now explicitly disables
    both preemption AND interrupts before calling schedule, and
    kernel_yield_post is removed (its job folded into kernel_yield).

  - New kernel/misc.c (+23) -- validate_stack_pointer_int(file,
    line): sanity-checks that the current stack frame's address is
    within the current task's kernel_stack page. Catches kernel
    code accidentally running on the wrong task's stack (the
    reproducer was 100% hit by the commit log's "making the wrong
    stack pointer problem 100% reproducible" bullet).

  - kernel/include/process.h (+6 / -6) -- task_state promoted from
    int constants to an enum (type-safe, easier to ASSERT on).

  - kernel/kb.c (+48 / -10) -- programs PS/2 typematic rate to the
    fastest setting; expands the E0 / E1 scancode handling, adds
    smoke tests, fixes a sync bug where a fast key-press sequence
    could lose scancodes.

  - kernel/tasklet.c (+30 / -30) -- fixes a synchronization bug in
    the producer-consumer loop where the tasklet-runner thread and
    add_tasklet_int() could race on the counter.

  - kernel/arch/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+14 / -7) -- assembly-level
    kernel_yield routine tightened (preserves the right callee-
    saved regs).

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+14 / -21), kernel/include/arch/
    generic_x86/x86_utils.h (+30 / -15), kernel/include/common_defs.h
    (+8 / -2), kernel/interrupts.c (+8 / -9), kernel/timer.c (+14 /
    -11), kernel/term.c (+17 / -1), kernel/debug_utils.c (+10 / -7),
    kernel/main.c (+10 / -5), kernel/process.c (+9), kernel/kmalloc.c
    (+5 / -2), kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (1 l.), kernel/arch/i386/
    gdt.c (1 l.), kernel/arch/i386/utils32.c (-8),
    kernel/include/arch/i386/arch_utils.h (+1),
    kernel/include/arch/i386/process_int.h (1 l.),
    kernel/include/paging.h (1 l.), usermode_init/init.c (+11 / -11)
    -- interrupt-handling invariants tightened: various ASSERT
    calls catch nested-interrupt / preemption-disable violations
    earlier.

  - New other_scripts/resolve_bt (28 l.) -- a script to turn a
    backtrace dump (frame addresses) into source:line via addr2line,
    rename from build_scripts/generate_coverage_report.

  - generate_coverage_report moves to other_scripts/ (file rename).

  - .travis.yml (1 l.), debug_run_qemu (1 l.), run_qemu (1 l.) --
    tiny.

Context (PR body + 15-bullet log):

  Most impactful is the kernel_yield fix (commented in the code) and
  the stack-pointer validator. Together they caught a class of
  subtle concurrency bugs that the May 2017 preemption work had
  exposed but never cleanly solved.

## dc55d2c8 -- fixing the nastly bug in disable_interrupts()

Commit: dc55d2c8d2...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed May 24 12:38:02 2017 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/x86_utils.h (+130 / -93) --
    complete rewrite of enable_interrupts / disable_interrupts /
    are_interrupts_enabled. New X86_EFLAGS_CF / ZF / SF / IF / DF /
    OF bit macros. The old are_interrupts_enabled_int() queried
    EFLAGS with a pushf-pop-movl sequence split across three
    asmVolatiles -- the compiler was free to reorder them.
    Consolidated into one asm block that atomically pushf-pops
    into a single operand. The old disable_interrupts() also
    incremented the counter AFTER the cli, which could race with
    a just-arriving interrupt -- now counter bump is first.

  - kernel/include/common_defs.h (+18 / -5) -- adds the EFLAGS bit
    defs to the kernel header proper.

Context (subject):

  This is the bug the stress test reproduced. The "nasty" qualifier
  is earned: multi-asmVolatile sequences against EFLAGS are
  notoriously broken -- GCC can hoist loads between them. The fix
  is standard Linux-kernel-style: one asm block, one operand, done.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 042884f4 -- fixing a nasty bug in get_eflags()

Commit: 042884f422...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed May 24 13:27:43 2017 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/x86_utils.h (+5 / -11) --
    get_eflags() had the same bug as are_interrupts_enabled: three
    separate asmVolatiles (pushf / pop %eax / movl %eax, %out).
    Replaced with one asm block. are_interrupts_enabled_int() now
    uses get_eflags() so there's one source of truth.

    compile flags. Prevents gcc from generating position-independent
    code sequences that break the pushf/pop pattern above (the
    author had hit this when the release build behaved differently
    than debug).

  function. Both bugs had been lurking since early 2017; the

## 8df049aa -- improving data in panic

Commit: 8df049aa96...

    frame-pointer gets moved to a different scope.

## f197d99c -- Changing the way the kernel removes dead kernel threads.

Commit: f197d99c70...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun May 28 11:53:51 2017 +0300

Message:

  Now, it does not use anymore the BASE_KERNEL_STACK and that solves
  at least one of the cases where the stack validation fails.
  Currently, the issue is not reproducible anymore.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/arch/i386/process32.c (+23 / -2) -- kthread_exit used to
    switch esp to a fixed BASE_KERNEL_STACK_ADDR and then jmp to
    the scheduler, relying on that "safe" stack area. Problem: the
    base kernel stack is also touched by the ISR path, so a
    concurrent interrupt could step on the zombie's fake stack
    frame. New approach: the exiting kthread schedules a tasklet
    (remove_dead_kthread_tasklet) on ANOTHER kernel thread, then
    calls schedule_outside_interrupt_context -- it goes to sleep
    as a ZOMBIE, and the tasklet (running on the tasklet-runner
    thread's own stack) does the actual kfree() of its task_info
    and kernel_stack pages.

  - kernel/sched.c (-8 / +2) -- the old "zombie kthread cleanup
    inside schedule()" code is gone (the tasklet handles it now).

  - kernel/include/arch/i386/arch_utils.h (1 l.),
    kernel/arch/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+2 / -1), kernel/main.c
    (+4 / -4) -- plumbing.

Context (subject + body):

  The stack-pointer-validation failures reappearing on real HW are
  narrowed to this specific cause: the ZOMBIE-stack trick was
  racing with interrupts. Moving cleanup to a dedicated kthread via
  tasklet avoids the whole ordering problem.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 1c2d91df -- Make interrupt code to restore the disable_interrupt_count to 0
   before returning

Commit: 1c2d91dfdb...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun May 28 13:20:01 2017 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/interrupts.c (+7 / -1) -- on handler exit, explicitly
    resets disable_interrupts_count = 0 before returning. The
    normal invariant is "count returns to what it was on entry",
    but if a handler path did unmatched disable/enable (bug or
    intentional workaround), the counter could leak across
    handlers. Forcing it to 0 on exit matches the hardware state
    (iret restores IF from the saved EFLAGS).

  - kernel/kb.c (+6 / -1), kernel/include/irq.h (1 l.) -- matching
    uses.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 8b7f71f4 -- Update README

Commit: 8b7f71f44c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed May 31 21:26:28 2017 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  README.md (+21 / -10) -- expanded project description. Adds a
  features list (paging, fork/exec, kmalloc buddy allocator,
  tasklets, kmutex/kcond, kernel_sleep) and a section clarifying
  what exOS is NOT (not a production kernel, not POSIX-compliant).
  Edited via GitHub web UI.

================================================================================
  ERA 5 -- Filesystems, EFI, and a self-hosted toolchain  (Sep 2017 - Jan 2018)
================================================================================

  After another ~3-month gap (the longest in project history to this
  point), exOS comes back with a very different focus: it's no longer
  mostly about kernel-internal scaffolding, but about becoming something
  you can run real programs on. In no particular order, this era lands:
  (1) generic data structures (AVL bintree + priority queue with
  thorough gtest coverage); (2) the list.h library diverges stylistically
  from its Linux-kernel original; (3) FAT16/32 read-only support
  including long-file-name decoding; (4) an EFI bootloader (gnu-efi
  based) so the kernel boots on UEFI-only machines; (5) massive build-
  system maturation -- scripts/ consolidation, self-downloaded
  CMake/nasm/mtools/gnu-efi, a bootlin x86-i686-buildroot cross-
  toolchain so kernel builds stop depending on host gcc-multilib,
  support for gcc 4.8 through 7, a Clang + Address Sanitizer CI job;
  (6) the first version of exvfs, the kernel's VFS layer, with an
  fs_handle_base + file_ops polymorphism inspired by Linux's
  struct file + file_operations. By the end of this era Tilck can
  mount a FAT filesystem from a memdisk, open files by path, read
  them through a unified VFS interface, and do all of this from a
  kernel built with its own pinned cross-toolchain.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d6a2db53 -- Introducing an implementation of an AVL tree and a priority
   queue (#39)

Commit: d6a2db5350...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Sep 3 23:17:36 2017 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  3-month gap since the previous commit. When activity resumes,
  generic data structures land first.

  - New kernel/avl_bintree.c (291 l.) + kernel/include/bintree.h
    (71 l.) -- AVL-balanced binary tree. API:
    bintree_insert_internal / find_internal / remove_internal take
    an object pointer, a compare function, and a
    bintree_offset (offset of the bintree_node field within the
    containing struct). Macros (bintree_insert / bintree_find /
    bintree_remove) compute the offset via OFFSET_OF so callers
    look like container-generic APIs. Find takes a separate
    objval_cmpfun because the search key is often not an object of
    the same type.

  - New kernel/pq.c (106 l.) + kernel/include/pq.h (28 l.) --
    min-heap priority queue of (void *data, int priority) pairs;
    push / pop O(log n). Internal array-backed heap with
    pqueue_init(capacity) preallocating.

  - New unittests/avl_bintree.cpp (494 l.) -- thorough gtest suite
    of the AVL tree: insert / find / remove / rotation invariants /
    stress-test against std::set.

  - New run_qemu_kvm (2 l.) -- qemu-system-i386 with -enable-kvm
    launcher; KVM was evidently too slow for some debug workflow
    before, now preferred for normal dev.

  - kernel/include/common_defs.h (+4), .vscode/settings.json
    (+6 / -4), .vscode/c_cpp_properties.json (+8 / -5) -- plumbing.

Context (guess -- no body, subject gives the what):

  Groundwork: the next months' work on timers, filesystems and
  more sophisticated scheduling will want efficient ordered
  containers. Landing AVL + priority queue with tests up-front
  lets future code just use them.

## 597ef13e -- Updating the implementation of list.h (#41)

Commit: 597ef13e1f...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>

Message:

  exOS and removes any similarities with the list.h in the linux
  kernel. Only the general idea of an intrusive doubly-linked list
  remained.

  - kernel/include/list.h (+42 / -53) -- fundamental rename
    pass: struct list_head -> struct list_node; list_head typedef
    -> list_node; LIST_HEAD_INIT -> make_list_node; INIT_LIST_HEAD
    -> list_node_init; list_add -> list_add_after; list_entry ->
    list_to_obj. Adds list_add_before. Drops the "similar to
    Linux's list.h" comment. Internal structure unchanged; pure
    rename for style consistency with rest of exOS.

  - kernel/arch/i386/idt.c (+23 / -23), kernel/sched.c (+5 / -5),
    kernel/arch/i386/process32.c (+2 / -2), kernel/include/arch/
    i386/process_int.h (+6 / -6), kernel/kcond.c (1 l.),
    kernel/kmutex.c (1 l.), kernel/process.c (1 l.) -- mechanical
    rename at call sites.

  - unittests/list_test.cpp (+20 / -19) -- test suite updated.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Style PR. The Linux-kernel list.h was adopted verbatim in
  commit 7046cca3 (PR #19); with the project having its own
  conventions by now, the structure is kept but names are
  brought in line with exOS's naming.

## cada89fe -- Introducing partial support for FAT16 and FAT32 (#42)

Commit: cada89fe14...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Sep 22 00:35:02 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change introduces in the kernel a partial read-only support
  for FAT16 and FAT32. The kernel now it is able to walk through
  the directory-tree of a FAT file-system and read a whole file.
  The walk-through across cluster chains is fully supported, both
  for directory entries and files. Only the "Long Directory
  Entries" feature has not been implemented yet, but it certainly
  will. Since this will be the FS used by the system, the 11 chars
  length-limit is not acceptable.

  Intentionally not implemented: handling of bad clusters and fall-
  back to other FATs different than the first one. That's clearly
  because this code has been designed to work only with FAT volumes
  in ramdisks, where bad clusters simply do not exist.

AI notes:

What changed:

  First real file-system support.

  - New kernel/fs/fat32.c (530 l.) + kernel/include/fs/fat32.h
    (165 l.) -- reads FAT12/16/32 volumes from a memory-mapped
    image. The header declares the full on-disk struct layout
    (BPB / fat16_header2 / fat32_header2 / fat_entry with
    bitfields for readonly/hidden/system/volume_id/directory/
    archive). The .c walks the directory tree, follows cluster
    chains (next-cluster lookup via the FAT table), reads full
    files into a caller-provided buffer. 8.3-only filenames for
    now (long-name / LFN is explicitly TODO in the subject).

  - New sysroot/ (test fixture tree): README, sbin/.gitignore,
    testdir/ with 3 subdirs of empty files, a file with a long
    name (which fat.c will refuse for now), and file.a /
    file.ab / file.abc for 8.3 edge cases.

  - build_scripts/build_fatpart.sh (+22 / -4) -- now mcopies
    sysroot/* into the FAT image instead of just copying init.

  - New unittests/fat32_test.cpp (61 l.) -- gtest harness loads a
    sample image and walks its contents, asserting expected
    filenames and contents.

  - kernel/main.c (+18 / -2) -- calls fat_dump_info() on the
    memdisk at boot as a demo.

  - kernel/include/string_util.c / .h (+23 / -6) -- helpers
    (strncmp, strcmp likely) that fat32.c needs.

  - CMakeLists.txt (+3 / -1), kernel/CMakeLists.txt (+1 / -1),
    README.md (1 l.) -- plumbing.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Foundational: the kernel can now read its own ramdisk as a FAT
  filesystem. Next step would be exec (load a program by name
  from the FS) and a VFS abstraction.

## a8b66b19 -- Introducing an EFI bootloader (#43)

Commit: a8b66b19ac...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Sep 30 23:03:37 2017 +0300

Message:

  This change introduces a EFI bootloader in the project. The
  generated image now has both the custom BIOS bootloader embedded
  in the MBR and an EFI loader in /EFI/BOOT/ (only for 64-bit
  machines). Limitations: unfortunately, I did not find a way to
  set the video card in text mode using the EFI APIs so I had to
  go back to real mode in switchmode.bin and execute int 0x10 for
  that, before booting the kernel. The problem is that this
  approach works only if the firmware is set to support also
  legacy bootloaders. In a pure-EFI environment, my code will go
  back to real mode, but int 0x10 just won't work.

  Therefore, the above limitation will remain for a long time
  unless:
    - I find a way to set the video card in text mode without int 0x10
    - I implement a graphical framebuffer in the kernel

AI notes:

What changed:

  First EFI boot path.

  - New bootloader/efi/efimain.c (263 l.) -- gnu-efi based EFI
    application. Wraps EFI BootServices calls with
    uefi_call_wrapper (the x86_64 ABI shim). Allocates specific
    physical pages via AllocatePages AllocateAddress, loads
    kernel.bin to 0x100000 and the FAT ramdisk to 0x08000000
    from the ESP filesystem, CRC32s both, calls
    ExitBootServices, then chain-loads switchmode.bin at
    0xC000.

  - New bootloader/efi/switchmode.asm (231 l.) -- 64-bit -> real-
    mode transition helper. Because exOS kernel is 32-bit, EFI
    drops us in long mode; this code constructs a fake GDT, drops
    to compatibility mode, then to real mode, runs int 0x10 to
    set 80x25 text video mode, and finally protected-mode jumps
    to the kernel at 0x100000.

  - New bootloader/efi/CMakeLists.txt (89 l.) -- gnu-efi compile
    options, -fpic -fshort-wchar -mno-red-zone -DEFI_FUNCTION_WRAPPER,
    objcopy to efi-app-x86_64 format. Produces BOOTX64.EFI placed
    under sysroot/EFI/BOOT/.

  - New sysroot/EFI/BOOT/.gitignore -- placeholder (BOOTX64.EFI
    drops here at build time).

  - bootloader/boot.asm (+50 / -51), bootloader/CMakeLists.txt
    (+5 / -1), CMakeLists.txt (+8 / -2) -- BIOS bootloader stays,
    builds both paths, final image has BIOS MBR + EFI ESP.

  - build_toolchain (+12 / -7) -- clones gnu-efi into toolchain/.

  - build_scripts/build_fatpart.sh (+12 / -3),
    build_scripts/create_empty_img_if_necessary.sh (1 l.),
    kernel/main.c (+6 / -2), README.md (1 l.) -- plumbing.

  - New run_qemu_usbdisk (2 l.), debug_run_qemu (1 l.), run_qemu
    (1 l.), run_qemu_kvm (1 l.),
    system_tests/run_system_test (+3 / -2) -- launcher scripts
    adjust to accept -bios OVMF.fd for EFI testing.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Huge step toward modern hardware support: exOS can now be booted
  on UEFI-only machines, not just legacy BIOS. The video-mode
  limitation is honest about the approach's fragility; the
  long-term fix (framebuffer driver) comes a few years later.

## 1bdb57c2 -- Making the unit tests build to use -Wno-register for C++ files

Commit: 1bdb57c2e2...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Dec 22 19:18:54 2017 +0200

Message:

  New C++1z compilers show a warning in case the 'register' keyword
  is used. Unit tests' C++ files include C headers files which use
  register since it is not deprecated in C. That causes the build
  of the 'gtests' target to fail, since -Werror is used.

AI notes:

What changed:

  unittests/CMakeLists.txt (+3 / -1) -- adds -Wno-register to the
  C++ flags for the gtests target. Kernel headers use register in
  C code; tests include those headers from C++17 which removed
  register.

Context (body explains):

  Compiler-upgrade compat fix. 3-month gap since the previous
  commit suggests the author upgraded gcc/g++ in the meantime.

## 638c7314 -- [build scripts] Make install_packages more powerful

Commit: 638c731419...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Dec 23 18:36:05 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  build_toolchain (+50 / -8) -- install_packages() rewritten:

    * packages list becomes a bash array instead of a space-
      separated string (easier to loop / query).
    * Detects the host distro from /etc/*release (accepts
      debian / ubuntu / mint); rejects others up-front with a
      list of required packages the user needs to install by
      hand.
    * Per-package dpkg -s check so already-installed packages
      aren't sudo-apt-installed redundantly. Also recomputed
      -- only the missing list is handed to apt.
    * Subject prefix "[build scripts]" introduces a convention
      that sticks for years.

Context (subject + commit-message style):

  This is also the first commit that uses the bracketed
  subject-prefix style which becomes Tilck's standard (see the
  intro block at the top of this file).

AI notes:

  install_debian_family() and a new install_fedora() that uses
  dnf / rpm -q and a fedora-specific package name list (qemu-

## de2ee591 -- [build scripts] Replace make_run with a fake Makefile

Commit: de2ee59184...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 24 11:34:14 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - Deleted make_run (5 l.) -- the trivial "cd build && make $@"
    wrapper.

  - New Makefile at repo root (25 l.) -- a "fake" Makefile whose
    targets (all, gtests, clean) forward to $(MAKE) -C build. If
    build/CMakeCache.txt doesn't exist, it first runs
    scripts/cmake_run. If toolchain/ doesn't exist, it $(error)s
    with instructions to run build_toolchain. Makes `make` just
    Do The Right Thing from the repo root even for new users.

  - scripts/build_toolchain (+2), .travis.yml (+3 / -3) --
    adjustments.

Context (subject):

  Same intent as before (run build from root), but now leveraging
  the fact that people default to typing `make` in a repo root.
  The stub Makefile discovers state and dispatches.

## 3e07ae3b -- [build scripts] Make build_toolchain to skip already built
   libraries

Commit: 3e07ae3b1e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 24 14:33:30 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  scripts/build_toolchain (+85 / -40) -- every build_* helper
  (build_cmake, build_lcov, build_dietlibc, build_musl,
  build_gtest, build_gnuefi) gains an "already exists?" guard.
  Re-running the script no longer rebuilds already-built
  dependencies; it prints "NOTE: Skipping <lib>" and moves on.
  Also wraps pushd/popd in silent versions so the script's
  output stays clean.

Context (subject):

  CI turnaround + iteration speedup. Previously re-running
  build_toolchain after tweaking one line took ~15+ minutes.
  Now re-running is near-instant unless the actual package
  changed. Foundation for the later "targeted install" -s flag.

## a08e2b56 -- [FAT32] Add support for long directory entries

Commit: a08e2b5694...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 24 20:52:59 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+140 / -25), kernel/include/fs/fat32.h
    (+34 / -6) -- implements the FAT LFN (Long File Name) scheme.
    fat_long_entry struct added (the union form that shares the
    same directory-entry slot when attributes == 0x0F). New
    fat_walk_dir_ctx keeps long_name_buf / long_name_size /
    long_name_chksum state across walk callbacks.
    fat_handle_long_dir_entry() decodes the UTF-16 characters
    (stored in three 2-byte segments LDIR_Name1/2/3) and
    reverse-orders them, since LFN entries are laid out backwards
    before the corresponding 8.3 entry. shortname_checksum()
    validates that the LFN set actually belongs to the
    following short entry; mismatches reset the buffer.

  - sysroot/testdir/This_is_a_file_with_a_veeeery_long_name.txt
    (+1 l.) -- test fixture now has content.

  - scripts/build_scripts/build_fatpart.sh (1 l.) -- mformat
    tweak.

  - unittests/fat32_test.cpp (+74 / -16) -- gtest coverage for the
    new long-name reader.

Context (subject + fat32 PR's earlier TODO):

  Closes the "long directory entries not implemented yet"
  explicit TODO from commit cada89fe. The kernel can now
  enumerate files with modern names like
  This_is_a_file_with_a_veeeery_long_name.txt instead of the
  8.3-mangled form.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 2a43538e -- [build] Use a locally downloaded x86-i686 toolchain

  reproducibility across distros.

    function: downloads and extracts a bootlin
    x86-i686--glibc--stable toolchain (i686-buildroot-linux-gnu-gcc
    etc.) into toolchain/. Pinned version 2017.05-1-1.

    CMAKE_C_COMPILER = $TCROOT/x86-i686--glibc--stable/bin/
    i686-buildroot-linux-gnu-gcc for the kernel. Kernel code is
    now compiled with a dedicated i686 cross-compiler instead of
    "host gcc + -m32 -march=i686".

    link paths tweaked (still uses musl + dietlibc against
    host gcc -m32 here; the arch split that moves userland to
    cross-compiler too comes later).

Context (subject):

  Instead of relying on gcc-multilib being available and
  producing -m32 output, the project now owns an actual
  cross-toolchain in toolchain/. First step toward the
  toolchain3/ layout that dominates from 2019 onward.

## 4cebfa34 -- [build] Move elf_kernel build in arch/CMakeList.txt

Commit: 4cebfa3448...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Dec 27 13:00:23 2017 +0200

Message:

  Reason: it's not possible in the same CMakeList.txt file to use
  two different C compilers. Previously the trick was done with
  the -m32 flag. Now, with a separated toolchain for x86 (i686)
  having two CMake files was mandatory.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (69 l.) -- owns the elf_kernel
    target (links the final kernel binary with the i686 cross-
    toolchain's ld / objcopy).

  - kernel/CMakeLists.txt (-61) -- strips the elf_kernel target
    definition; keeps only the per-module kernel libraries compiled
    with the cross-compiler.

Context (subject + body):

  CMake can only have one CMAKE_C_COMPILER per directory scope.
  Since the kernel + kernel unit tests need DIFFERENT compilers
  (cross vs host), they must live in different CMakeLists files
  now. This is the split that enables the tests to continue
  building against host gcc.

## 5b7e20e7 -- Starting to work on exvfs

Commit: 5b7e20e7e5...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Dec 27 18:36:43 2017 +0200

Message:

  BONUS[1]: fixed build problem with errno.h
  BONUS[2]: adding long file name validation in FAT32 code

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/fs/exvfs.c (1 l.) -- empty placeholder.

  - New kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (29 l.) -- first sketch of
    exOS's VFS layer. Header comment explicitly flags it as a
    "toy VFS", not attempting parity with Linux's. Declares
    typedef void *fs_file_handle and function-pointer types
    func_open(const char *) / func_close(fs_file_handle), plus
    a partial struct {char name[16]; ...} for registering a FS.

  - kernel/include/errno.h renamed to kernel/include/exos_errno.h
    -- avoids collision with musl's errno.h when both are on
    include path.

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+53 / -3) + kernel/include/fs/fat32.h
    (+5) -- LFN reading now validates the checksum of the
    preceding short-name entry against the accumulated long-name
    buffer (the FAT LFN spec requires it). Malformed chains are
    discarded.

  - kernel/syscalls.c (+1 / -1) -- uses the renamed exos_errno.h.

## 3954fe7f -- [FS] Implementing fat_read()

Commit: 3954fe7fc8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Dec 30 12:17:32 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+68 / -20) -- fat_read(handle, buf,
    count) reads up to count bytes starting at the handle's
    current seek offset. Correctly walks the cluster chain,
    handles reads that span cluster boundaries, clamps at
    end-of-file, updates the seek offset. Works for both FAT16

## 93283a75 -- [FS] Implemented fseek() and ftell() for FAT32

Commit: 93283a7508...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 31 19:23:35 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/fs/fat32.c (+92 / -1) -- fat_fseek(handle, off, whence)
  and fat_ftell(handle). fseek walks forward through the cluster
  chain from the handle's current position until the cumulative
  byte count reaches the target; for backwards seeks it restarts
  from the file's first cluster. SEEK_SET / SEEK_CUR / SEEK_END
  supported. kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (+8 / -1) -- API addition.

## 03a2c73d -- [FS] Implement exvfs wrappers

Commit: 03a2c73d43...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jan 2 19:51:53 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  First generic VFS dispatch layer.

  - kernel/fs/exvfs.c (+106 / -6) -- exvfs_open(path) /
    exvfs_close(handle) / exvfs_read / exvfs_fseek (plus
    friends) dispatch to the appropriate filesystem via its
    registered mountpoint. Resolution uses a new
    check_mountpoint_match(mp, path) helper that mandates
    mountpoints end in '/' and verifies the match stops at a
    path-component boundary. mountpoint_add now ASSERTs
    path[strlen-1] == '/' (invariant).

  - kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (+21) -- public API.

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+6 / -10) -- adjusts to the new exvfs
    entry points (fat_open etc. get called via
    filesystem.fops).

  - kernel/include/common_defs.h (+7) -- adds STATIC macro
    (expands to static in release, empty in test so the
    function is exported for gtest access).

  - New unittests/exvfs_test.cpp (60 l.) -- tests
    check_mountpoint_match and basic mount/open/read round-trip.

Context (guess -- subject says "wrappers"):

  Before this commit, callers had to know which FS to dispatch
  to (they called fat32_open directly). After this, opening by
  path "dispatches" based on the registered mount. Foundation
  for later mounts of multiple filesystems.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 37c65f56 -- [FS] Improve the fat32/exvfs tests by adding load_once_file()

## 71ee9987 -- [FS] Allow fseek() to go past the end of the file

Commit: 71ee9987e8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Jan 3 22:06:08 2018 +0200

Message:

  BONUS: fixing 2 bugs in mountpoint_remove().

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+18 / -2) -- fat_fseek no longer clamps
    the target offset at file size; POSIX lseek allows seeking
    past EOF (subsequent writes create sparse files; reads
    return 0 bytes). Tilck won't write to FAT soon, but the
    read-past-eof semantics match lseek now.

  - kernel/fs/exvfs.c (+16 / -4) -- fixes mountpoint_remove: (1)
    the kfree call was using the wrong argument (mps instead of
    mps[i]); (2) the NOT_REACHED at the end was incorrectly
    unconditional -- it should only fire if no matching mount
    was found, not after a successful removal.

  - kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (1 l.), unittests/exvfs_test.cpp
    (+12 / -14) -- signature adjustment and tests.

## 86b5350d -- [FS] Fixing some bugs in seek()

Commit: 86b5350d21...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Jan 4 15:41:45 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+7 / -14) -- lseek simplification: instead
    of manually walking clusters for forward seeks and reseting
    for backward seeks, it always resets to first_cluster and
    walks to the target offset. Slower for random access but
    eliminates the class of "off-by-one in cluster boundary"
    bugs the previous version had.

  - kernel/fs/exvfs.c (+5) -- param validation (negative offset
    in SEEK_SET gets -EINVAL).

  - kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (1 l.) -- sig cleanup.

## 04b1e765 -- [FS] Refactoring the exvfs interface

Commit: 04b1e76575...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Jan 4 18:27:44 2018 +0200

Message:

  - Removed fhandle
  - Moved read, write, seek in file_ops
  - Make all the file handles to include the members of
    fs_handle_base

AI notes:

What changed:

  Big structural cleanup of the nascent VFS.

  - kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (+32 / -19) -- retires fhandle
    typedef (opaque void*). Introduces fs_handle_base, an
    embedded-head struct with fs_handle_base *next, filesystem
    *fs, and file_ops *fops, so every FS-specific handle must
    embed an fs_handle_base as its first member (classic Linux-
    style "open class" polymorphism via first-field trick).

  - New file_ops struct (read / write / seek / close function
    pointers) -- replaces the scattered per-call func_*
    pointers on filesystem. exvfs_read/write/seek now do one
    dispatch through h->fops->read(h, ...).

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (+39 / -38) -- fat_handle's first member
    is fs_handle_base; fat32 registers a static file_ops table
    and assigns it into h->fops at open time.

  - kernel/include/fs/fat32.h (+5), kernel/fs/exvfs.c (+13 / -15),
    unittests/exvfs_test.cpp (+3 / -5), unittests/fat32_test.cpp
    (+6 / -4) -- matching updates.

Context (PR body):

  This is the shape that becomes Tilck's kernel VFS long-term:
  a handle is always "pointer to a struct whose first field is
  fs_handle_base", and operations dispatch via h->fops. Same
  pattern the Linux kernel uses for file * / struct file_operations.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 2f16785e -- [build toolchain] Make the build of dietlibc to fully succeed

Commit: 2f16785e7d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Jan 4 20:16:55 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  scripts/build_toolchain (+16 / -9) -- the dietlibc build had
  been using set +e (ignore failures) since mid-2017 because
  one cross-compile step reliably errored even when it
  produced usable output. Root cause: dietlibc's Makefile
  invokes strip on a host binary that's actually a 32-bit ELF
  (cross-built), and strip fails when strip-flags don't match.
  Fix: pre-install the toolchain's strip onto PATH before
  invoking dietlibc's make; dietlibc's build now completes
  without the set +e workaround.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## a40e851a -- [FS] Make the elf loader to use exvfs_read()

Commit: a40e851a63...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jan 5 18:16:57 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/elf_loader.c (+33 / -24) -- rewritten to
    exvfs_lseek + exvfs_read chunk-by-chunk rather than
    memcpy'ing from a mapped byte pointer. Previously the
    loader assumed the ELF was already contiguously mapped in
    memory. Now it reads headers, then per-segment, using
    file-ops, so the source doesn't need to be mmap-backed.

  - kernel/fs/exvfs.c (+2 / -2), kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h
    (+2 / -2) -- signature refinement (ssize_t count returns).

Context (guess -- subject):

  Paves the way for loading ELFs from non-memdisk filesystems
  later (real block devices won't have the "mapped contiguously"
  property).

## c975b4ee -- Remove process_int.h

Commit: c975b4ee34...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jan 6 13:35:54 2018 +0200

Message:

  This change aims to provide a more convenient arch-abstraction
  mechanism in the kernel by extending hal.h and by moving the
  content of process_int.h, in particular the struct task_info
  into process.h: actually only a few of its members (like regs)
  are arch-dependent and #ifdefs in headers like hal.h could
  solve the problem. Now, when the noarch code can use task_info
  members expect regs members, which are arch-specific and that's
  exactly what we wanted. In special cases like interrupts.c that
  need just to get the interrupt number from regs, a convenient
  wrapper called regs_intnum() has been added in hal.h. For
  non-supported architectures, the wrapper has a stub
  implementation.

AI notes:

What changed:

  HAL-layer refactor. Moves the arch-specific parts out of
  headers that shouldn't need them.

  - kernel/include/arch/i386/process_int.h deleted (-46) --
    struct task_info and its friends no longer live under
    arch/. kernel/include/process.h (+52) picks up the full
    task_info definition; the only arch-dependent part (regs
    state_regs) uses #ifdef __i386__ to include the right
    arch_utils.h.

  - kernel/include/hal.h (+27 / -8) -- adds regs_intnum(regs*)
    accessor wrapper so arch-independent code (interrupts.c
    etc.) doesn't need to know the regs struct layout. Arch
    stubs provided for uncompiled archs.

  - kernel/include/arch/i386/arch_utils.h (-10),
    kernel/include/irq.h (+2 / -6), kernel/include/sync.h
    (+2 / -3), kernel/interrupts.c (+5 / -10),
    kernel/debug_utils.c (+2 / -2), kernel/elf_loader.c (-2),
    kernel/misc.c (+1), kernel/process.c (1 l.),
    kernel/sched.c (+2 / -147), kernel/tasklet.c (+1) -- remove
    redundant #include of the deleted header.

  - kernel/arch/i386/process32.c (+154 / -6) -- the i386-specific
    task_info fields (regs) live here in arch-specific
    constructors / accessors.

  - unittests/generic_mocks.c (+2) -- mock for regs_intnum.

Context (PR body):

  process_int.h had become a leaking abstraction: many of its
  fields weren't actually i386-specific. Promoting task_info to
  the generic header layer lets arch-independent code write
  current->pid without conditional compilation; only accesses
  to state_regs still need arch-awareness (and those go through
  regs_intnum).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    (-11) -- plumbing.

Context (subject):

  Closes the "stage3 needs its own print infrastructure" side-
  quest: stage3 can now call printk directly, sharing the same
  implementation the kernel uses. Diagnostic output becomes
  uniform across the boot path.

## 68b7826e -- [bootloader] Make the bootloader to load the kernel from the
   FATPART

Commit: 68b7826e58...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jan 9 21:18:28 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/stage3.c (+9 / -6) -- walks the FAT image mounted
    in memory to find kernel.bin, reads it into the kernel's
    load address (0x100000), then jumps there. Stage2 had been
    loading the kernel from a hardcoded sector; now it only
    loads stage3, and stage3 finds the kernel by name.

  - bootloader/boot.asm (+5 / -13) -- stage2 no longer needs
    its own kernel-loading logic. Shrinks.

  - CMakeLists.txt (-4), kernel/include/arch/i386/arch_utils.h
    (+2 / -1), kernel/include/hal.h (1 l.) -- plumbing.

Context (guess -- subject):

  Milestone: a filesystem-aware bootloader. From this point, you
  can put a different kernel in the FAT image and stage3 will
  load whichever one you named kernel.bin -- no more rebuilding
  the disk image from scratch for every kernel change.

## e6ec5b48 -- [bootloader] Make the bootloader lighter

Commit: e6ec5b48e4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jan 9 21:25:42 2018 +0200

Message:

  This change splits the fat32.c file by renaming it to
  fat32_base.c and by moving its unnecessary (for the bootloader)
  functions back to the kernel.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - common/fat32.c renamed to common/fat32_base.c (-399 lines
    out of the original; keeps the mount / directory walk / read
    core).

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c reappears (+404) -- gets the kernel-only
    helpers back (fat_handle file-ops wrappers, open-by-path
    with exvfs dispatch, seek semantics).

  - bootloader/naive_malloc.c deleted (-21) -- was only needed
    by the handle/seek code that's now kernel-only. Stage3
    doesn't need a malloc.

  - bootloader/CMakeLists.txt (+6 / -2) -- compiles only
    common/fat32_base.c, shrinking stage3's binary.

Context (body):

  Stage3 lives in a tight memory budget (fits in a few sectors
  before the kernel). Splitting fat32 into "core" (stage3 + kernel
  share) vs "kernel-only" (fat_handle + exvfs wrappers) brings
  stage3 back under that budget.

## 331acc7f -- [bootloader] Loading elf kernel works!

Commit: 331acc7f45...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jan 13 13:13:30 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  Milestone: the BIOS bootloader (stage3) now loads kernel.bin
  as a real ELF32 file, not a raw binary.

  - bootloader/stage3.c (+86 / -5) -- implements an ELF loader:
    reads Elf32_Ehdr + Elf32_Phdrs from the FAT file, loops over
    PT_LOAD segments, copies p_filesz bytes to p_vaddr, zero-
    fills up to p_memsz, jumps to e_entry. Scaled-down copy of
    the kernel-side loader; no paging (kernel runs at identity-
    mapped physical address right after boot).

  - common/fat32_base.c (+254) -- gains helpers (fat_entry_ptr,
    fat_cluster_to_lba etc.) that stage3 needs for ELF
    extraction.

  - kernel/fs/fat32.c (-247) -- the helpers moved above leave
    the kernel-side file.

  - .vscode/settings.json (+2 / -1), kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt
    (+4 / -1) -- the kernel build now produces a real ELF
    (kernel.elf) stripped to kernel.bin earlier -- no longer
    just a flat binary.

Context (subject):

  First time the kernel is loaded as an ELF rather than a raw
  blob. Precondition for symbol-based debugging and for
  eventually having a .bss section larger than 0 (uninitialized
  globals no longer waste disk space).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 6b8f923b -- [bootloader] Strip debug info from the elf kernel

Commit: 6b8f923b9c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jan 13 13:20:16 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (+4 / -2) -- after the elf_kernel
    target links, a strip step produces kernel.bin (the file
    stage3 loads) and keeps the unstripped kernel.elf around as
    the debug artifact. Saves ~300 KB in the FAT image.

  - CMakeLists.txt (1 l.), scripts/build_scripts/build_fatpart
    (1 l.), bootloader/stage3.c (1 l.) -- point at the right
    artifact names.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## c3592598 -- [kernel] Removing unnecessary ={0} initializations of global
   variables

Commit: c359259815...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jan 13 13:32:32 2018 +0200

Message:

  Now that the kernel is an ELF binary and the bootloader
  supports that, uninitialized global variables just go into
  BSS without wasting space in kernel's binary.

AI notes:

What changed:

  Reversal of the BSS workaround from the pre-ELF era.

  - kernel/include/common_defs.h (-23) -- deletes the "every
    global must have ={0} so it goes to .data" convention.

  - kernel/arch/i386/gdt.c (-3), kernel/arch/i386/idt.c
    (-2), kernel/kmalloc.c (-2), kernel/tasklet.c (-5),
    kernel/fs/exvfs.c (1 l.), kernel/arch/generic_x86/term.c
    (-5), kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (1 l.),
    kernel/arch/i386/process32.c (1 l.),
    unittests/exvfs_test.cpp (-2) -- drop the ={0} initializers
    on zero-valued globals. Compiler puts them back in .bss,
    the ELF kernel loader zero-fills at load time.

  - CMakeLists.txt (+2 / -2), kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt
    (+3 / -5) -- removes -fno-zero-initialized-in-bss flag
    that enforced the workaround; removes the
    build_scripts/bss_checker invocation (scalar .bss is
    now expected and fine).

Context (body explains):

  ELF loaders handle .bss natively, so the workaround that
  forced everything into .data is obsolete. Kernel image
  shrinks by a few KB.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 6ff9241c -- [paging] Removing a dirty hack for the allocation of the kernel
   page dir

Commit: 6ff9241ca3...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Jan 25 20:45:59 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

    had been allocated via a special "early" path (pre-
    pageframe_allocator) because the page allocator itself

## 27c870ab -- [paging] Add an anonymous union for using PG_* bit flags

Commit: 27c870ab9e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jan 26 18:50:10 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/include/arch/i386/paging_int.h (+66 / -20) -- page_t
    and page_dir_entry_t gain an anonymous union: the old
    bitfield-per-field form stays, but a parallel flat
    uint32_t raw; field makes it ergonomic to set multiple
    flags at once via PG_PRESENT | PG_RW | PG_US etc. New
    PG_* defines enumerate the bit positions.

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+32 / -27) -- call sites switch
    from .present = 1; .rw = 1; ... to .raw = PG_PRESENT |
    PG_RW | .... Shorter, more readable.

    kernel/include/self_tests/self_tests.h (+1) -- tiny.

## 2f119469 -- [build] Add support for GNU ASM

Commit: 2f11946999...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 28 15:59:54 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - CMakeLists.txt (+2 / -1) -- enables GNU AS (ASM) as a CMake
    language alongside NASM. AS rules use the cross-toolchain's
    i686-buildroot-linux-gnu-as.

  - kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (+17 / -3) -- adds a separate
    target for .S (preprocessed GAS source) files, distinct
    from .asm (nasm source).

  - bootloader/CMakeLists.txt (+11), bootloader/efi/CMakeLists.txt
    (+1 / -1) -- match.

Context (subject):

  Foundation for moving the kernel's assembler files from
  nasm/Intel syntax to GAS/Intel syntax. GAS can be driven by
  the cross-toolchain's gcc + `-x assembler-with-cpp` which
  lets #include and #define work in asm files -- not supported
  by nasm.

## b9c25b5c -- Re-write kernelAsm.asm to work with GAS but with Intel syntax

Commit: b9c25b5c45...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 28 18:05:03 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  Major: kernel's assembly split from nasm to GAS.

  - New kernel/arch/i386/entry.S (280 l.) -- replaces the main
    body of kernelAsm.asm (context_switch, IRQ / ISR stubs,
    pusha/iret plumbing). Uses GAS's .intel_syntax noprefix so
    the code reads identical to the nasm version but can be
    preprocessed with cpp.

  - New kernel/arch/i386/irq_handlers.S (29 l.) + isr_handlers.S
    (63 l.) -- the repetitive 16 irq / 32 isr entry points,
    generated via .irp / .endr macros (GAS loops) instead of
    copy-paste.

  - kernel/arch/i386/kernelAsm.asm (-657) -- near-complete
    gutting; only a tiny stub remains for symbols that still
    need nasm (removed in the next commit).

  - kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (+10 / -2) -- compiles the .S
    files via the ASM rules from the previous commit.

Context (subject):

  .S + GAS macros collapse ~460 lines of copy-paste IRQ/ISR
  stubs into ~90 lines of .irp iteration. Also allows using
  C-style #defines for constants (segment selectors, error
  codes) that were previously duplicated.

## 2a2e791a -- [bootloader] Re-write boot.asm for GAS as gas_boot.S

Commit: 2a2e791a90...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Feb 1 19:28:47 2018 +0200

Message:

  The code generated in both cases is IDENTICAL (checked with
  objdump + diff) except for two MOVs for which GAS used an
  equivalent encoding.
  See: https://www.strchr.com/machine_code_redundancy

AI notes:

What changed:

  Bootloader stage1+stage2 fully migrate from nasm to GAS.

  - New bootloader/gas_boot.S (940 l.) -- hand-ported line-by-
    line from bootloader/boot.asm. .intel_syntax throughout; BPB
    (BIOS Parameter Block) embedded via .byte directives at the
    right offset; stage2 inlined via .incbin or direct code.

  - bootloader/CMakeLists.txt (+17 / -4) -- switches the build
    rule to GAS. boot.asm stays in the tree for reference but
    is no longer linked.

  - kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (1 l.) -- minor.

Context (body):

  The author explicitly verified that the produced binary is
  byte-for-byte identical (modulo two equivalent MOV encodings)
  by running objdump + diff. No subtle bugs from the port. This
  finishes the nasm -> GAS migration across the whole project:
  kernel, bootloader stage1+2, and stage3 all now use GAS.

## f17233a6 -- Moving stdint.h in common/system_headers

Commit: f17233a636...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Feb 2 20:40:07 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  Rename: common/include/stdint.h ->
  common/system_headers/stdint.h. The system_headers/ directory
  is for shim headers whose name matches a standard libc
  header -- they need to be found before the real ones on the

  unittests/CMakeLists.txt (+4 / -2) -- include-path tweaks.

  exOS needs to shadow a system header (stdint.h, stddef.h,
  etc.), it goes under common/system_headers/.

## 881c8157 -- [BUILD] Removing NASM from the toolchain

Commit: 881c815757...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Feb 3 10:52:31 2018 +0200

Message:

  NASM is an amazing assembler but, unfortunately, always will
  be that "additional tool" that is needed, which does not
  perfectly integrate with the classic gcc-toolchain. For that
  reason, the NASM files have been re-written to work with the
  GNU assembler, but they continue to use the INTEL syntax.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - CMakeLists.txt (-7) -- drops the project(exos C CXX ASM_NASM)
    ASM_NASM dependency; CMake no longer needs nasm as a
    recognized language.

  - scripts/build_toolchain (1 l.) -- removes the build_nasm
    function call from the default pipeline (the function
    itself stays in the file as a no-op for a while).

Context (body):

  Wraps up the nasm retirement. With GAS everywhere, the build
  is entirely driven by gcc + binutils; one fewer tool in the
  toolchain graph.

AI notes:

    script for stage3 specifying .text / .rodata / .data / .bss
    layout and the start address. Replaces implicit layout via
    ld -Ttext=<addr>.

  C, assembly, and rodata strings that need to sit in
  specific memory regions.

## 9ed01a79 -- working on making load a ramdisk bigger than 31 MB to work

Commit: 9ed01a79e9...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Feb 3 18:44:10 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/boot.S (+32 / -24) -- the CHS-based disk read
    loop in stage2 had an implicit upper bound from the BIOS
    int 13h interface (cylinder field is 10 bits, so past a
    certain disk size the read address wraps). Rewritten to
    use LBA (int 13h AH=0x42 -- extended disk services) for
    reads past the BIOS CHS limit. Falls back to CHS when the
    target is in range (for maximum BIOS compat).

  - common/include/config.h (+3 / -3) -- RAMDISK_SIZE raised
    from 31 MB toward 35 MB target; the constant in the commit
    is actually an intermediate value during the debugging of
    the LBA path.

Context (subject):

  Ramdisk size limit was a hard one: BIOS's classic CHS
  interface couldn't describe locations past ~8 GB on the disk,
  and for a memdisk even 32 MB was already hitting edge cases
  on some BIOSes. LBA extension fixes it.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 795313f4 -- saving progress: problems with checksum

Commit: 795313f4c1...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Feb 4 12:17:26 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/main.c (+20 / -1) -- adds CRC32 of the loaded
    ramdisk at kernel entry and compares against a hardcoded
    expected value; prints "CRC MISMATCH" if they differ. Mid-
    debug instrumentation.

  - bootloader/boot.S (+1 / -3), common/include/config.h
    (+4 / -11) -- cleanup.

Context (subject):

  Explicitly a WIP checkpoint; the LBA-based read was
  corrupting bytes near the end of the ramdisk on some QEMU
  configurations. The next commit fixes several root causes.

## 435bfa22 -- [bootloader] Fixing several bugs

Commit: 435bfa2215...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Feb 4 19:20:51 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/boot.S (+113 / -97) -- large delta closing the
    bugs the previous checkpoint surfaced:

      * LBA-packet was being set with an off-by-one sector
        count at the final iteration (loading 1 extra sector
        of garbage that then CRC-mismatched).
      * ES:BX buffer address overflowed segment when the read
        size crossed a 64K boundary; now advances ES every 64K
        of cumulative read.
      * Fallback path from LBA to CHS activated incorrectly on
        some BIOS that returned AH=0 but had actually
        ignored the LBA request; added a stricter check.

  - common/include/config.h (-22) -- removes now-unused
    constants that were duplicating disk-geometry values
    (LBA makes them irrelevant).

  - kernel/main.c (+18 / -8) -- updates the CRC baseline now
    that loading is correct.

  - run_qemu (+3 / -2) -- passes explicit qemu flags useful
    for testing the LBA path.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## b31bfb46 -- [paging] Make the paging_pageframe_allocator to use a separate
   bitfield

Commit: b31bfb46ed...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Feb 19 12:47:48 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/paging_pageframe_allocator.c (68 l.) -- splits
    the paging-reserved allocator out of the main
    pageframe_allocator.c into its own file with its own
    independent bitmap. Removes the "two bitmaps inside one
    function" entanglement that was fragile.

  - kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (-67) -- loses the paging
    branch entirely; becomes a pure general-purpose pageframe
    allocator.

  - common/include/utils.h (+13) -- bitset_set / bitset_clear
    / bitset_is_set helpers shared by both allocators.

  - kernel/include/paging.h (+4 / -4) -- signature tweaks.

Context (subject):

  The split makes both allocators simpler to reason about and
  individually unit-testable (no shared mutable state).

## 386d1490 -- [pageframe_allocator] Remove useless volatile attrs

## e2a12e35 -- [pageframe_allocator] Remove an useless optimization

Commit: e2a12e3508...

## 45fb92ee -- [pageframe_allocator] Make MAX_MEM_SIZE_MB = 1024

Commit: 45fb92ee7a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 20 13:05:48 2018 +0200

Message:

  After measuring allocator's performance with several tests,
  it came out that its performance does not really depend so
  much on MAX_MEM_SIZE_MB.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (+29 / -6) -- MAX_MEM_SIZE_MB
    grows from 128 MiB to 1024 MiB (1 GiB). Bitmap size grows
    proportionally (1 GiB / 4 KiB / 8 = 32 KiB bitmap). The
    perf tests established that scan-to-find-free-bit stays
    dominated by locality, not raw bitmap length.

  - kernel/include/paging.h (+5 / -5) -- PAGES_BIT_FIELD_ELEMS
    recomputed.

  - kernel/self_tests/perftests.c (+80 / -46) -- reworked for
    the larger address space.

  - unittests/general_pageframe_allocator_test.cpp (+3 / -3)
    -- tests updated.

Context (body):

  Before this, Tilck couldn't handle more than 128 MiB of RAM
  without the allocator's bitmap overflow-wrapping. Now it
  accepts up to 1 GiB.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 0a7b6f47 -- [pageframe_allocator] Minor changes

## c6467e06 -- [pageframe_allocator] Implemented unaligned 128 KB block alloc

Commit: c6467e0636...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 20 14:01:47 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (+38 / -15) -- adds
  alloc_pageframes_aligned() supporting runs of 32 contiguous
  pages (= 128 KiB) at arbitrary offsets. Previously a multi-
  page alloc assumed 128 KiB-aligned start; the aligned
  version finds a 32-bit-zero u32 in the bitmap. Now an
  unaligned variant searches for any N contiguous free bits
  across u32 boundaries.

Context (subject):

  Large physical allocations (e.g. DMA buffers, contiguous
  framebuffer memory) sometimes need arbitrary offset not
  aligned to the bitmap-word size.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 37b4ff70 -- [pageframe_allocator] Re-write alloc_32_pageframes

Commit: 37b4ff70b2...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 20 18:55:52 2018 +0200

Message:

  Now the unaligned fall-back is much faster.

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (+23 / -42) -- net shrink.
  alloc_32_pageframes rewritten: instead of separate aligned /
  unaligned code paths, a single loop that OR-combines two
  adjacent u32 words and shifts to find a 32-bit-wide zero
  window. Shorter, and the perftest reports ~2x speedup on
  the mixed-workload case.

Context (body + subject):

  End of the unaligned-alloc arc from commits 394-397.
  Production-quality version.

## df871411 -- [kmalloc/pageframe_allocator] Add alloc-8 and make virtual_* to
   use it

Commit: df8714110c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 20 20:58:30 2018 +0200

Message:

  This change introduces alloc_8_pageframes() and
  free_8_pageframes() in the pageframe allocator and re-writes
  kbasic_virtual_alloc() and kbasic_virtual_free() to use it.
  Now those functions will never allocate pageframes one by one.
  They support only 32 and 8 as page count. If a physically
  contiguous block of memory is not found, they'll fail.
  The only exception is the case of 32 pages: in case of a
  failure, an attempt will be made to allocate the 32 pageframes
  in groups of 8. Since kbasic_virtual_free() cannot know if the
  32 pageframes are contiguous or not, it always frees them in
  groups of 8. This seems the best trade-off between the
  flexibility of the single pageframe allocation and the
  performance of the always-contiguous allocations.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (+32 / -5) -- new
    alloc_8_pageframes (8 contiguous pages = 32 KiB) and
    free_8_pageframes. Uses a 1-byte mask in the bitmap u32;
    4x faster to scan than individual-page alloc.

  - kernel/kmalloc_util.c (+64 / -43) -- kbasic_virtual_alloc
    accepts only page_count == 8 or 32. For 32, tries
    contiguous first; on failure, splits into 4x8-page
    allocs. kbasic_virtual_free always does 8-at-a-time frees
    (since the original contiguity state is unknown).

  - kernel/include/paging.h (+2) -- declarations.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Commits to a simpler allocation model: kmalloc buys pages
  in 8- or 32-blocks only. Gives up the "any count" flexibility
  in exchange for much faster alloc on the hot path. The
  kmalloc buddy allocator above this is already block-
  oriented, so the restriction is invisible to normal users.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 973d8e15 -- [kmalloc] bool has_some_free_space => full

Commit: 973d8e15cc...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 21 16:47:28 2018 +0200

Message:

  By changing the name and the meaning of that bool in the
  block_node bitfield, the value of new_node is just 8 zeros.
  This allows the function evenually_allocate_page_for_node()
  to use bzero() instead of memset(). Also, bzero() has been
  optimized a for the case of len divisible by 4.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+26 / -26) -- block_node.has_some_free_space
    is renamed block_node.full and its meaning is inverted
    (true = completely allocated, false = some free space).
    A fresh node is now all-zero (previously had to have
    has_some_free_space = 1 set), so zero-initialization is
    correct -- which lets the allocator use a much faster
    bzero() for new meta-data pages.

  - kernel/include/string_util.h (+9 / -1) -- bzero gains a
    fast path using rep stosl (4-byte stores) when len is
    divisible by 4, falling back to rep stosb for the tail.

## 92783962 -- [kmalloc] Minor optimizations by precalculating two log2
   variables

Commit: 92783962d3...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 21 17:27:19 2018 +0200

Message:

  The variables were heap_data_size_log2 and
  alloc_block_size_log2.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+15 / -13) -- the log2_for_power_of_2
    calls for HEAP_DATA_SIZE and ALLOC_BLOCK_SIZE were being
    repeated inside the hot path. Promoted to file-scope
    constants (heap_data_size_log2, alloc_block_size_log2).
    Visible speed win -- these are CONSTEXPR but gcc
    wasn't hoisting them out of the loop at -O2.

  - common/include/utils.h (+9 / -22) -- log2_for_power_of_2
    simplified to rely on __builtin_clz on the fast path,
    which gcc can evaluate at compile time.

## 4f6c8074 -- [kmalloc] Micro-optimization: remove the 'vaddr' from the stack

Commit: 4f6c8074dd...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 21 17:58:14 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/kmalloc.c (+13 / -15) -- the iterative allocator's
  stack of 32-byte triples (node_size, vaddr, node) shrinks
  to 24 bytes per entry by dropping vaddr. vaddr is re-
  derivable from (node, node_size) via node_to_ptr(). Less
  stack cache pressure on the hot path.

## 8bd3127b -- [bootloader] Make stage3_entry.S to contain both _start and main

Commit: 8bd3127bc8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Feb 22 11:37:54 2018 +0200

Message:

  For some strange reason, even if stage3_entry.S was passed to
  the linker before anything else, the linker decided to put
  the C function main() at the very beginning of .text. In the
  linker script its explicitly stated that the entry symbol is
  '_start', but that was not enough. I haven't found yet a way
  to force symbols order using the linker script. Therefore,
  the hacky workaround is just put both _start and main in
  stage3_entry.S and just call the C main function
  bootloader_main.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/stage3_entry.S (+5 / -3) -- adds a tiny wrapper
    main: that immediately tail-calls bootloader_main. The
    linker will place this main first in .text (before the
    actual C main symbol in stage3.c gets a chance).

  - bootloader/stage3.c (1 l.) -- C function renamed main ->
    bootloader_main.

  - bootloader/linker_script.ld (-2) -- removes an obsolete
    ENTRY() directive.

Context (body explicitly flags this as a workaround):

  Ideal fix would be to put .text._start in a SECTIONS { } ahead
  of .text.* -- but getting ld to honor that for a -e _start
  executable was tricky enough that the author punted on it.
